    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";

            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||

            }

          callback();

    }

<span id="freeTextContainer11937139072995420369">From one of the twentieth century’s master novelists, the author of the classic All Quiet on the Western Front, comes Heaven Has No Favorites, a bittersweet story of unconventional love that sweeps across Europe.<br/> <br/>Lillian is charming, beautiful . . . and slowly dying of consumption. But she doesn’t wish to end her days in a hospital in the Alps. She wants to see Paris again</span>
  <span id="freeText11937139072995420369" style="display:none">From one of the twentieth century’s master novelists, the author of the classic All Quiet on the Western Front, comes Heaven Has No Favorites, a bittersweet story of unconventional love that sweeps across Europe.<br /> <br />Lillian is charming, beautiful . . . and slowly dying of consumption. But she doesn’t wish to end her days in a hospital in the Alps. She wants to see Paris again, then Venice—to live frivolously for as long as possible. She might die on the road, she might not, but before she goes, she wants a chance at life.<br /> <br />Clerfayt, a race-car driver, tempts fate every time he’s behind the wheel. A man with no illusions about chance, he is powerfully drawn to a woman who can look death in the eye and laugh. Together, he and Lillian make an unusual pair, living only for the moment, without regard for the future. It’s a perfect arrangement—until one of them begins to fall in love.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11937139072995420369" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer596939348" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2397798283144845010"><b>Heaven Has no Favorites: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://readwithstyle.wordpress.com/2013/04/24/heaven-has-no-favorites-erich-maria-remarque/'>http://readwithstyle.wordpress.com/20...</a></b><br/><br/>A few nights back my mother asked me who my most favorite authors were. Among the names I listed was of course Erich Maria Remarque. She had read most of his novels as a student but she found him way to depressing and she suggested it was about time I stopped being so suicidal and read something more cheerful.<br/><br/>When I went to bed I started thinking about what she said. Having read 7 novels from Erich Maria Remarque, I agree he always</span>
  <span id="freeText2397798283144845010" style="display:none"><b>Heaven Has no Favorites: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://readwithstyle.wordpress.com/2013/04/24/heaven-has-no-favorites-erich-maria-remarque/">http://readwithstyle.wordpress.com/20...</a></b><br /><br />A few nights back my mother asked me who my most favorite authors were. Among the names I listed was of course Erich Maria Remarque. She had read most of his novels as a student but she found him way to depressing and she suggested it was about time I stopped being so suicidal and read something more cheerful.<br /><br />When I went to bed I started thinking about what she said. Having read 7 novels from Erich Maria Remarque, I agree he always creates a gloomy atmosphere of despair and hopelessness. His characters are exemplary sufferers – scarred by one of the two World Wars, missing family members and friends, fighting a terminal illness, suffering from depression and all of the above. His characters are extremely philosophical – they further their suffering by thinking over and over again about the meaning of life and death, the existence of happiness, the relationship between people, the past and the future, the nature of love. His characters drink and eat. I know, this sounds stupid, but one of the aspects about Remarque I have noticed is that he pays special attention to the food and drinks accompanying his characters. Alcohol has that special function in his works (and in life in general) – it alleviates the pain and it prompts the characters to even more philosophical endeavors across the human mind. They drink when they celebrate, they drink when they suffer and they drink when they love. And yet in this suicidal atmosphere Erich Maria Remarque always includes a spark of hope. No matter the circumstances, his characters manage to fall in love – completely, utterly, hopelessly.<br /><br />Read more: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://readwithstyle.wordpress.com/2013/04/24/heaven-has-no-favorites-erich-maria-remarque/">http://readwithstyle.wordpress.com/20...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="2397798283144845010" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1710268066" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1085368159790758218">I found this old book in an antique shop and it was a real treat. It tells the story of Lillian who is slowly dying and how she leaves a hospital in search of living out her final days in full. She meets Clerfayt, a race car driver. Essentially they each live for the moment and fall in love. We are all living an instant at a time, who know if we have a long life and does the future extend only to the next breath we each take. Who knows? </span>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer179248746" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer10377007457432856080">As if gazing down a long corridor, Lillian saw what remained, what could still possibly happen between them. It was a corridor that narrowed steadily, and did not have an exit. She could not walk along it. Others, who had more time,probably could do it. Not she. And in love, there was no turning back. You could never begin afresh; what had happened remained in your blood. Clerfayt could never again be as he had been with her. He could be that way with any other woman, but not with her. What they</span>
  <span id="freeText10377007457432856080" style="display:none">As if gazing down a long corridor, Lillian saw what remained, what could still possibly happen between them. It was a corridor that narrowed steadily, and did not have an exit. She could not walk along it. Others, who had more time,probably could do it. Not she. And in love, there was no turning back. You could never begin afresh; what had happened remained in your blood. Clerfayt could never again be as he had been with her. He could be that way with any other woman, but not with her. What they had had could no more be recalled than time, and no sacrifice, no readiness, no amount of good will would suffice. That was the sad, the inexorable law. Lillian knew it, and for that reason she wanted to leave. The remnant of her life was her whole life—but in Clerfayt’s life it was only a small part. It therefore depended entirely on her, not on Clerfayt. The scales were too uneven; what would be only an episode in his life, although he did not believe it now, was the end for her. She could not throw it away; she knew that now. She felt no regret; she had too little time even for that. But she felt a clarity that resembled the morning’s clarity. And with this clarity the last mists of misunderstanding vanished. She felt the small, sharp joy of decision. And—strangely—with the decision her tenderness returned—for she was now out of danger.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10377007457432856080" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/68353308" />
    <a title="Jana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2296903-jana"><img alt="Jana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1387230362p2/2296903.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2296903-jana?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer68353308" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10101669360775209448">The language at first seems a bit outdated, but Remarque wrote this book almost 50 years ago. In a time when people were different as well. Had more manners at least, if nothing else. In my mind I was juggling with this fact, 50 years ago. Remarque was internationally well known writer, and nowadays, he is forgotten. But this book is great. There were times when I felt disconnected with the characters and I was frowning because I was expecting so much of it. But I didn’t understand it, and I was</span>
  <span id="freeText10101669360775209448" style="display:none">The language at first seems a bit outdated, but Remarque wrote this book almost 50 years ago. In a time when people were different as well. Had more manners at least, if nothing else. In my mind I was juggling with this fact, 50 years ago. Remarque was internationally well known writer, and nowadays, he is forgotten. But this book is great. There were times when I felt disconnected with the characters and I was frowning because I was expecting so much of it. But I didn’t understand it, and I was rushing. <br /><br />The title is brutal and appropriate. It’s not like Remarque will force you and make you love his Lillian and Clerfayt. He is not impressed with you as a reader, he is not going to suck up, he lets you observe, but he leaves you on the other side of the fence. He engages you, and then shocks you. But in a really subtle way. Remarque is not a provocative writer. <br /><br />He is believable. Along the way, he writes these gems of philosophy, life truths and viewpoints. He connects their stories in a full circle and you understand why Lillian is completely closed and torn and why Clerfayt needs wind and space. And thus why heaven has no favorites.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10101669360775209448" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2846893813" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2846893813" />
    <a title="Shoti" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/53373701-shoti"><img alt="Shoti" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1477072777p2/53373701.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2846893813?book_show_action=true">Jun 07, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shoti" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shoti" href="/user/show/53373701-shoti">Shoti</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53373701-shoti?shelf=classic-20th-century">classic-20th-century</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2846893813" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11310257375424503540">Death, death and DEATH!<br/><br/>It is 1949 and Europe is trying to recover from the nightmarish years of WW II. The novel portrays the improbable love of Lillian, a 24-year-old charming lady suffering from terminal tuberculosis, and Clerfayt, a 44-year-old professional car racer. Lillian is fully aware that time is quickly running out for her and she determinedly appreciates every moment and experience life can still offer as a gift. She is the breathing manifestation of Carpe Diem, freed from the shackl</span>
  <span id="freeText11310257375424503540" style="display:none">Death, death and DEATH!<br /><br />It is 1949 and Europe is trying to recover from the nightmarish years of WW II. The novel portrays the improbable love of Lillian, a 24-year-old charming lady suffering from terminal tuberculosis, and Clerfayt, a 44-year-old professional car racer. Lillian is fully aware that time is quickly running out for her and she determinedly appreciates every moment and experience life can still offer as a gift. She is the breathing manifestation of Carpe Diem, freed from the shackles of long-term commitments and everyday banalities in a manner which is the unique privilege of those who don’t care a lot about tomorrow. Lillian doesn’t have the luxury to take life and health for granted like most people. Her fascination with the honest joy of living each moment for itself irresistibly seduces Clerfayt and other men. They don’t fully understand what attracts them to Lillian but they instinctively admire her nevertheless. <br /><br />Remarque creates a bittersweet atmosphere where lighter episodes and dialogues are constantly overshadowed by the unspeakable truth. The novel has some beautifully written touching scenes. I am always quick to draw upon my cold heart and cynical mind against attacks of syrupy romanticism – that was not needed here which is grand testimony to Remarque’s brilliance. Heaven Has No Favorites is a sound reminder that as long as one is healthy and has someone to love, the remaining individual challenges, concerns and problems presented by life might eventually be no more than trifling inconveniences...</span>
  <a data-text-id="11310257375424503540" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Lillian and Clerfayt's love is unconventional and tragic, yet beautiful and touching. A brilliant masterpiece.</span>

<div id="review_1513946523" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1513946523" />
    <a title="Amanda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8291622-amanda"><img alt="Amanda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1332255842p2/8291622.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1513946523?book_show_action=true">Jan 17, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amanda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amanda" href="/user/show/8291622-amanda">Amanda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/28589569-heaven-has-no-favorites">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1513946523" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5926775547671680502">I received this book from an acquaintance nearly a decade ago with the following note attached:<br/><br/>"Dear Amanda,<br/> Best wishes for the holidays! I hope you will enjoy this book as much as I did. I tried to find a new copy of the book but it is apparently out of print, so I am sending you my own copy. I also have another copy in German. I always felt that my attitude to this book was unique. I read it differently than others because of my constant battle with health. And there was always certain sadnes</span>
  <span id="freeText5926775547671680502" style="display:none">I received this book from an acquaintance nearly a decade ago with the following note attached:<br /><br />"Dear Amanda,<br /> Best wishes for the holidays! I hope you will enjoy this book as much as I did. I tried to find a new copy of the book but it is apparently out of print, so I am sending you my own copy. I also have another copy in German. I always felt that my attitude to this book was unique. I read it differently than others because of my constant battle with health. And there was always certain sadness in that uniqueness. I know that you will read this book through the same lense of life experiences that I did. That's why it was so important for me to share this book with you. As to the New Year's wishes, I hope we can meet for the new year and have only good news to share.<br />Love, Natalia"<br /><br />Very soon thereafter, my health took a turn for the worse and I cut ties with many, many people and situations...even many previously good ones. At least once every year I would try to read HEAVEN HAS NO FAVORITES, but it was like reopening a vast, deep wound...I couldn't get past my own hurt to the heart of the matter. And I'm grateful for being so kind to myself then as to set it aside till now.<br /><br />Again the annual culling of my bookshelves came with the new year and finally, after reading another gifted book with another personal inscription, I turned again to Remarque. And this time it caught me, latched on hard, and would not let me go until, here I am, ten days later having completed it cover-to-cover. I read passages, and reread them, and reread them again. <br /><br />Remarque's work is both a compelling personal story and indeed the fictional reflection of my "life experiences" that Natalia had presumed it to be. In fact, I believe it ever more relatable now than it would have been had I read it straight through upon receipt. I needed the years to go "From Brescia to Brescia." Thank you Natalia...wishing you the best wherever you are.<br /><br /><br />**Favorite HEAVEN HAS NO FAVORITES Quotes**<br /><br />(p78-79) She felt that she was trembling. She studied Clerfayt. He asked no questions. I don’t have to explain anything to him, she thought. He takes me at my word. What to me is the decision of my life is to him only the kind of ordinary decision people make every day. Perhaps he doesn’t even think me particularly sick; I suppose it takes a car smash to convince him that someone is really incapacitated. She felt to her surprise as if a burden she had borne for years were sliding from her shoulders. Here was the first person for years who was not concerned about her illness. It made her happy in a strange way. It was as if she had crossed a frontier hitherto impassable to her. Her sickness, which had always been like an opaque window between herself and the world, no longer existed, at least for the moment. Instead, life lay outspread before her, breathtakingly clear and wide, flooded with moonlight; life with clouds and valleys and happenings. And she belonged to it, she was no longer excluded from it; she stood like all others, the healthy people, at the starting point, a burning, crackling torch in her hand, ready for the steep drop, the rush down and into life. What had Clerfayt said once? That the most desirable thing in life was to be able to choose your own death, because then death could not kill you like a rat or extinguish you, suffocate you, when you were not ready. She was ready. She trembled, but she was ready.<br /><br />(p96-97) Tired! she thought. Monotonous! Can’t this healthy specimen of life see that I am quivering all over? Doesn’t he understand what’s going on in me? Can’t he feel that my frozen picture of the world has suddenly thawed and is moving and talking, that the rain is talking, the wet rocks are talking and the valley with its shadows and lights, and the road? Doesn’t he have any idea that I shall never again be so at one with them as I am now — as if I were lying in the cradle and in the arms of an unknown god, frightened and still as trustful as a young bird, and yet already knowing that all this will exist for me only this one time, that I am losing it even as I possess it and it possesses me, this road and these villages, these dark trucks in front of the roadside inns, this singing behind lighted windows, the guitars, the grey-and-silver sky, and these names — Osogna, Cresciano, Claro, Castione, and Bellinzona — scarcely red and already subsiding behind me like shadows, as if they had never been? Doesn’t he see that I am a sieve losing what it receives, not a basket that collects what is put into it? Doesn’t he notice that I can scarcely speak because my heart is swelling so, and that among the few names it feels, his is one too, but that all of them really mean only one thing again and again: life? <br /><br />(p125) ‘I think you don’t care about anything, do you?’ he asked.<br /> She turned towards him and smiled. ‘In a very intense way, that’s true.’<br /> ‘I thought so. What’s done this to you?’<br /> I know that I am dying, she thought, feeling the light of the street lamps gliding over her face. I know that more definitely than you, that’s all, and so I hear the things that are mere noise to you as messages and cries and carols of joy, and feel the things that are commonplace to you as mercies and great gifts.<br /><br />(p144) Levali offered his arm. ’Going away is not always so simple — when one takes oneself along.’<br /> ‘It is always terribly simple when one knows that there are limits to the desire for possession — and that one cannot hold on to anything, not even oneself—‘<br /> They walked towards the music. ‘Is there nothing you want to possess?’ Levali asked.<br /> ‘There’s too much I want to possess,’ Lillian replied. ‘And so, nothing.’<br /><br />(p170-171) If you escaped death frequently, you were reborn just as frequently, and each time with a deeper gratitude —so long as you dropped the idea of having a claim upon life.<br /><br />(p218) She grew calm. She still did not know what she would do, but that she could do something made everything less unbearable. She did not fear unhappiness; she had lived too long with it and by it. She also did not fear happiness, as did so many of those who thought they were seeking it. What she feared was the prison of mediocrity. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5926775547671680502" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer197772664" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3332914804965962748">A sad and meandering book about a pair of lovers on the edge of death. One is a race-car driver who survived the horrors of a Nazi camp and the other has tuberculosis. The book deals with characters who do not wallow in the past but instead try to live their best life on the way to their inevitable deaths. Each has a a searing honesty about themselves, which is how they connect to each other, and leading to some rather pithy philosophical moments. While the book lacks some focus in the fourth ac</span>
  <span id="freeText3332914804965962748" style="display:none">A sad and meandering book about a pair of lovers on the edge of death. One is a race-car driver who survived the horrors of a Nazi camp and the other has tuberculosis. The book deals with characters who do not wallow in the past but instead try to live their best life on the way to their inevitable deaths. Each has a a searing honesty about themselves, which is how they connect to each other, and leading to some rather pithy philosophical moments. While the book lacks some focus in the fourth act, it has a powerful final act. Most of all, it is not cheap or maudlin in its emotions, which means when a passage tugs at the heart it is earned and all the more powerful.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3332914804965962748" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_994497065" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/994497065" />
    <a title="Greg Brozeit" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26552534-greg-brozeit"><img alt="Greg Brozeit" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544324486p2/26552534.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/994497065?book_show_action=true">Jul 12, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Greg Brozeit" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Greg Brozeit" href="/user/show/26552534-greg-brozeit">Greg Brozeit</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Taschenbuch 9783462027273" href="/book/show/4558981-der-himmel-kennt-keine-g-nstlinge">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26552534-greg-brozeit?shelf=deutsch">deutsch</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26552534-greg-brozeit?shelf=german-fiction">german-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26552534-greg-brozeit?shelf=remarque">remarque</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer994497065" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12283788682523893040">What does it mean to love? What does it mean to live? Remarque does not answer the questions, but this novel prods us to think more deeply about them.<br/><br/>Most of Remarque's novels illuminate how individuals lived through various episodes of German history between WWI and the end of WWII. This story, the next-to-last novel published during Remarque's lifetime, breaks that mold. Although it is set in post-WWII Europe and there are inklings of a survived past during the war, this story moves beyond the</span>
  <span id="freeText12283788682523893040" style="display:none">What does it mean to love? What does it mean to live? Remarque does not answer the questions, but this novel prods us to think more deeply about them.<br /><br />Most of Remarque's novels illuminate how individuals lived through various episodes of German history between WWI and the end of WWII. This story, the next-to-last novel published during Remarque's lifetime, breaks that mold. Although it is set in post-WWII Europe and there are inklings of a survived past during the war, this story moves beyond the history of the time.<br /><br />Clerfayt, a racecar driver, meets Lillian, a patient at a sanatorium in Switzerland. She wants to leave and Clerfayt takes her with him to Paris, beginning an unpredictable journey together. Clerfayt is another Remarque character-type: remote, individualistic and enigmatic. He finds his match in Lillian although their destinies are as different as their fates are similar. A bittersweet story written by a master of literature.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12283788682523893040" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer12860628037446476418">My favorite book that will always have a special place in my heart.<br/><br/>So much beauty and truth in the words of the characters. How could a person write something so beautiful and still so heart-breaking? I love Lillian and Clerfayt. And Remarque for writing this book. He shows us the most intimate thoughts of these two humans and you can't help but love them and understand them.   <span id="freeText12860628037446476418" style="display:none">My favorite book that will always have a special place in my heart.<br /><br />So much beauty and truth in the words of the characters. How could a person write something so beautiful and still so heart-breaking? I love Lillian and Clerfayt. And Remarque for writing this book. He shows us the most intimate thoughts of these two humans and you can't help but love them and understand them. It is like you are sitting in Paris restaurant, eating lobsters and drinking wine with them in their own world. Like Lillian's dresses are yours as well. It makes you want to live your life to the fullest. And travel. And eat good food. And listen to jazz.<br /><br />The truth is that I have listened to it as an audiobook (three times already) and it was read very well. I think that maybe that helped me get into the story more... Every time I feel low, I listen to random parts of this book and it helps.<br /><br />Love, love, love &lt;3</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17866902837920496276">Well this was disappointing. To sum it up, up until the end, (a typical Remarque ending) nothing happens in this book. I would say that this could more accurately be classified as a travelers guide. Only the places, town names, coffee shop names, hotels... change, the rest is all the same. Listing of what they ate, and what they drank followed by a deep philosophical conversation about how life is unappreciated. I found the main character to be quite annoying, striking me more as a rebellious an</span>
  <span id="freeText17866902837920496276" style="display:none">Well this was disappointing. To sum it up, up until the end, (a typical Remarque ending) nothing happens in this book. I would say that this could more accurately be classified as a travelers guide. Only the places, town names, coffee shop names, hotels... change, the rest is all the same. Listing of what they ate, and what they drank followed by a deep philosophical conversation about how life is unappreciated. I found the main character to be quite annoying, striking me more as a rebellious and irresponsible teenager then a woman I could sympathize with.<br /><br />I simply didn't enjoy reading this book.</span>

    <a title="Kirila" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21391122-kirila"><img alt="Kirila" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1407439597p2/21391122.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1003465862?book_show_action=true">Sep 19, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kirila" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kirila" href="/user/show/21391122-kirila">Kirila</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1003465862" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9821847825349262840">You know how the book is going to end from the very beginning. But you still hope. I enjoyed following the relationship between the main characters and how it changed as they got closer. It's an interesting observation that Remarque makes. You fall for somebody the way they are and they like you for who you are, but then you try to change yourself and the other person because you think that's how you will like and be liked better. But in reality you just take away the parts you fell in love with</span>
  <span id="freeText9821847825349262840" style="display:none">You know how the book is going to end from the very beginning. But you still hope. I enjoyed following the relationship between the main characters and how it changed as they got closer. It's an interesting observation that Remarque makes. You fall for somebody the way they are and they like you for who you are, but then you try to change yourself and the other person because you think that's how you will like and be liked better. But in reality you just take away the parts you fell in love with.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9821847825349262840" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1883773942" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1883773942" />
    <a title="Anet Kissova" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35142697-anet-kissova"><img alt="Anet Kissova" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1411134010p2/35142697.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1883773942?book_show_action=true">Jan 18, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anet Kissova" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anet Kissova" href="/user/show/35142697-anet-kissova">Anet Kissova</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1883773942" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14003554459258953474">Found this little precious in a garage. It was a bit harder to get through the beginning. Took me about 30 pages to get interested. But after that I got totally catched, impressed and couldn´t stop reading. Dozens of deep quotes, love story behind. But nothing pathetic. Set in the age after war, characters have manners, classy. Book is showing the beauty of living a life in present, not worrying about future. I LIKE! Spoiler: Unexpected ending :) </span>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('cbc6klhvzatVhPAMdjFfU5WPKdhgCYvC+sT1jpmw+ksgVclO3F1Q1icGnlHvP9ZVp9qkHFQ3twCVAZIo34OLGA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('X+NiXOppr6R3runakyFzVTG9EnlkS2tR4gS/R6bc6jcOAZGAblsy2QUsh4cKL/pTA+ifvVB1V5ONwdjh4O+bZA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

Естествено тая съпоставка - по пътя на контраста - води до по-релефни очертания.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/4116.Erich_Maria_Remarque">About Erich Maria Remarque</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/4116.Erich_Maria_Remarque"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1207351165p3/4116.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/4116.Erich_Maria_Remarque">Erich Maria Remarque
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
3,854
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer239048300022635752">Erich Maria Remarque (pen name of Erich Paul Remark) is one of the best known and most widely read authors of German literature in the twentieth century. <br/><br/>Remarque's biography is essentially marked and his writing fundamentally influenced by German history of the twentieth century: Childhood and youth in imperial Osnabrück, World War I, the Weimar Republic, and most of all his exile in Switzerland </span>
  <span id="freeText239048300022635752" style="display:none">Erich Maria Remarque (pen name of Erich Paul Remark) is one of the best known and most widely read authors of German literature in the twentieth century. <br /><br />Remarque's biography is essentially marked and his writing fundamentally influenced by German history of the twentieth century: Childhood and youth in imperial Osnabrück, World War I, the Weimar Republic, and most of all his exile in Switzerland and the United States. With the novel All Quiet On the Western Front, first published in 1929, Remarque attained world-wide recognition continuing today. <br /><br />Examples of his other novels also internationally published are: The Road Back (1931), Three Comrades (1936, 38), Arch of Triumph (1945), The Black Obelisk (1956), and Night in Lisbon (1962). <br /><br />Remarque's novels have been translated in more than fifty languages; globally the total edition comes up to several million copies. <br /><br />The complete works of Remarque are both highly interrelated with his Osnabrück background and speaking thematically of a critical examination of German history, whereby the preservation of human dignity and humanity in times of oppression, terror and war always was at the forefront of his literary creation. <br /><br />AKA:<br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/17900575._________________" title="Έριχ Μαρία Ρεμάρκ" rel="nofollow noopener">Έριχ Μαρία Ρεμάρκ</a> (Greek)<br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8106923._________________" title="Эрих Мария Ремарк" rel="nofollow noopener">Эрих Мария Ремарк</a> (Russian)</span>
  <a data-text-id="239048300022635752" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>

<div class="clear"></div></div></div><div class="bigBoxBottom"></div></div>
